something you are explicitly loading it into memory which can cascade into huge overheads depending on how something is referenced between 
classes. Interfaces don't care if that class exists or not. If the event is fired and there isn't a receiver it doesn't care either way. Very 
pro move\r\na class should really only care about itself until something else invokes it, its just good architectural design\r\ndon't fully 
reject casts, tho\r\nthey are incredibly useful\r\nbut use them wisely\r\nan example might be \"Plugin A has class X,Y,Z and casts to all 
those actors to make communication straight forward\" but \"Plugin B needs to trigger class Y's event, so you send an interface event to 
Plugin A manager to communicate to its own systems\"\r\nas a game dev, make systems. Not a game per se. The game is the outcome of those 
systems\r\ntrust me, you can go overboard with interfaces\r\nits not fun\r\nGhostRider — 5/8/2026 11:48 AM\r\nWhen you call Cast To, the 
entire code is always loaded into your other blueprint, which is unnecessary and causes the game to lag. Therefore, use an interface so you 
only call what you need.\r\ndb — 5/8/2026 4:42 PM\r\nNo it’s not completely unnecessary sometimes, it depends on what\n<truncated 3210
